-64 -                      ANNEX 3.1
ANNEX 3.1: TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR TEPGC
ORGANIZATIONAL RESTRUCTURING AND FINANCIAL
MANAGEMENT SYSTEMS
A. BACKGROUND AND OBJECTIVES
1.    Tuoketuo Electric Power Generating Company (TEPGC) is a Limited Liability
Company, founded in May 1996 by the North China Power Group Company (NCPGC),
Inner Mongolia Electric Power Company (IMEPC), and Beijing International Electric
Power Development Investment Company (BIEPDIC). Their respective ownership
shares are NCPGC 51 percent, IMEPC 34 percent, and BIEPDIC 15 percent of the
shares.
2.    TEPGC is one of the beneficiaries of the proposed World Bank loan to finance the
first phase of the Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant (2x600 MW units). The output from the
station is to be purchased by NCPGC and fed into the Jing-Jin-Tang grid, intended
specifically to satisfy the increasing demand in Beijing and its environs.
3.    The formation of TEPGC as an independent nonutility generator is a significant
organizational development in the Chinese power sector.  It represents a major
undertaking to meet the operational challenges of power sector reforms initiated by the
Chinese Govermnent. One of the major objectives of these reforms is to establish a
modem  enterprise system  characterized by clear definition of property rights,
autonomous management, commercial orientation, financial independence, and
separation of government ownership  and regulatory  functions from  enterprise
management.  The reforms are mainly based on:  (a) new accounting regulations,
promulgated by the Ministry of Finance and in effect since July 1, 1994, and (b) the
improved enterprise policy and governance framework defined by the Company Law
enacted in July 1994.
4.    To achieve these objectives, the Chinese Government and the World Bank jointly
developed an implementation program of sector reforms that stresses full corporatization
and greater autonomy and accountability of power enterprises.' The reform strategy is
intended to improve the operational efficiency and increase the market orientation of the
power sector.
5.    Like most state-owned enterprises, TEPGC is likely to be faced with the
following problems: (a) government interference in management, administrative and
China Power Sector Reform: Toward Competition and Improved Performance, Report No. 12929-
CHA, Document of the World Bank, September 15, 1994.



-65 -                      ANNEX 3.1
operational decisions reflecting the former central planning orientation of the economy;
(b) lack of full accountability of managers stemming from an inadequate, highly
centralized decision-making and nonavailability of timely and accurate financial
information at different operational activity levels; and (c) lack of transparency of the
financial situation: financial statements may not provide full disclosure of TEPGC's
financial position.
6.    This technical assistance activity is financed through the Tuoketuo thermal power
project and is designed to address the above-mentioned organizational and financial
issues. It stresses the strengthening of internal organizational and management practices,
and the introduction of appropriate accounting, budgeting and financial management
systems. The technical assistance provides not only for consulting services but also
training of TEPGC's staff and managers in China and abroad to ensure successful
implementation of the study recommendations and developed systems. To achieve the
full benefits of organizational reform and improved financial reporting and monitoring
systems, it is proposed to carry out the project in three distinct but fully integrated phases:
Phase I: Preparation Phase
7.    Comprising a comprehensive review of the organizational structure, management
practices, and financial/accounting practices and reporting systems in TEPGC. Particular
attention would be paid to the division of responsibilities, flow of information and quality
of reporting, and budgeting and accounting systems and procedures.
Phase II: Development Phase
8.    Comprising the development of a suitable organizational structure, design of the
required accounting and financial and budgeting systems to meet the need of efficient
management and decentralized decision-making, and preparation of a detailed plan for
implementation.
Phase III: Implementation Phase
9.   Implementation of the organizational structure and financial systems approved by
TEPGC including computer, software and training needs.
B. SCOPE OF WORK
10.   The project will include, but not necessarily be limited to, the following tasks:
Phase I: Preparation Phase
11.   During the first phase, the consultants are required to carry out a detailed
assessment of the current organizational structure and financial management practices,
considering the experience of selected nonutility generation entities. The scope of this
review will include:
(a)   Internal organization, operating and administrative procedures with
particular attention to the responsibilities of the planned functional units



-66 -                      ANNEX 3.1
their relations. Aspects to be examined would be overlap in lines of
responsibility, excessive centralization of decision-making, and
organizational deficiencies;
(b)   Accounting procedures, documentation, reporting formats and the nature
of financial transactions between the various departments and units of
TEPGC;
(c)   Assessment of Cost Accounting, Financial Planning, Budgeting, and
Internal Audit systems and procedures;
(d)   Evaluation  of performance monitoring  systems: establishment of
performance targets and indicators, methods for communicating,
controlling and monitoring them.
Phase II: Development Phase
12.   During the second phase, the consultants will, jointly with TEPGC, develop an
organizational structure and related management, accounting, financial, control and
reporting systems that address TEPGC's specific requirements. Useful features of other
nonutility generating enterprise models in other countries and China will be incorporated.
The work in this phase is organized in three subactivities:
Organizational and Management Structure
13.   The consultants, jointly with TEPGC, will provide definitions of the functional
boundaries and responsibilities of the Board of Directors and the management of TEPGC
and the role of the President, Vice Presidents and their relationship with operational
departments. They will also provide redefinitions of the functional boundaries and
responsibilities of the different departments, work units and subsidiaries.  Special
attention should be given TEPGC's main functions. The recommended organization
should also prepare TEPGC for its role as a major player in a more competitive power
sector.
(a)   Definition of interorganizational relationships, communication  and
reporting channels between the different units.
(b)   Assistance in the preparation of an Operational Manual that describes the
organizational structure, functional boundaries, job descriptions,
communication and reporting channels, limits of authority, etc. Special
attention should be given to accounting and financial units.
(c)   Recommendation of optimal staffing and preparation of job description
and qualification requirements for all posts of reasonable importance in the
recommended organizational structure.



- 67 -                     ANNEX 3.1
(d)   Improvement of the planning and control of the operational support
functions such as maintenance, work planning/management, procurement,
quality control, transportation, personnel management, etc.
Accounting Systems and Practices
(a)   Definition of accounting units and activities clearly identifying cost and
profit centers, reporting requirements, formats for information flow and
frequency of information exchange. This task will develop a basic design
for the new financial and accounting information system. It is of crucial
importance that this basic design of the financial and accounting
management information system be totally consistent with the proposed
reorganization of business processes and procedures.
(b)   Development of a Standard Financial Accounting System and general
accounts classification detailing balance sheets, income statements, and
cash flow statements. This should include policies and system procedures,
recommended principles for accounting classification, and follow-up
methods. The system should develop and provide for the timely collection
of accounts receivable and settlement of accounts payable. It should also
contain standards for depreciation for fixed asset accounting.
(c)   Assistance in the preparation of an Accounting Manual setting forth a
coded chart of accounts, detailing and describing balance sheet accounts,
income accounts, functional and department accounts, cost/profit centers,
objective accounts, policies, standard procedure instructions, report
formats (including an inventory of reports describing their purpose and
method of preparation, assigning responsibilities for preparation,
timetable, frequency and distribution lists), use of capital and expense
budget programs (including guidelines distinguishing capital items and
items charges directly to expense).
(d)   Improvement of the Internal Control and Audit System through approval
and audit procedures, internal review systems-especially for purchasing,
inventory and stores, handling of cash, and payroll.
Budgeting and Performance-Based Management Information Systems
(a)   Defining the process of setting performance targets, and the systems for
controlling and monitoring them in practice. This would include policies
and procedures, related analytical techniques, and mechanical tools to
ensure project planning, formulation, justification, management and
control of budgets, including analysis of budget variances.
(b)   Procedures to integrate MIS with the cost accounting system so that it can
generate information for assigning responsibility, measure labor and input
productivity against standards, analyze and control cost variances (i.e.,



-68 -                      ANNEX 3.1
input and labor price and quantity, efficiency, overheads, and capacity
variances) from standards. This should facilitate the determination of the
level of profitability of TEPGC so that pricing decisions can be taken with
the full knowledge of costs.
(c)   Develop a Financial Planning system, including the introduction of
operational objectives and planned allocation of resources in the form of
Operating Expense Budgets and Capital Expenditure Budgets, and the
frequency for issuance. The budgeting system should be coordinated with
the financial accounts in order to reconcile budget variances with financial
figures.
(d)   Define the planning and control of operational support functions or central
service functions, such as, maintenance and work planning/preparation,
materials management, procurement, quality control, transportation,
personnel management, etc.
14.   The consultant will prepare a detailed scope of tasks and a clearly defined
implementation strategy. The implementation strategy will be divided into actions and
targets with a timetable and should identify the priorities of and sequence in
organizational change and systems development.
Phase III: Implementation
15.   During this phase, the consultant will assist TEPGC in implementing the
recommended changes in organizational structure, business practices, financial
management and reporting systems. The work will include:
(a)   assistance in implementing the organizational structure and organizing

(b)   assistance in selecting and installing suitable hardware and software,
especially a new general ledger package and appropriate centralized/
distributed computer systems to be linked to desktop terminals.
(c)   identification of staffing and skills required to implement the new
financial/accounting systems and appropriate in-house, external training
programs, and assistance in preparation of training manuals.

the end of each phase of the process.

by the Steering Committee and/or TEPGC management. All reporting will be in Chinese
and English. The Consultant will provide ten (10) copies of all interim and final reports.

- 70 -                     ANNEX 3.2
ANNEX 3.2: TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR NCPGC
ACCOUNTING AND FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT SYSTEMS
A. BACKGROUND AND OBJECTIVES
1.    The North China Power Group Company (NCPGC) is one of the largest
companies in China. It has 47 wholly-owned subsidiary enterprises, 55 enterprises with a
controlling interest and 29 enterprises with a minority stake. NCPGC runs and operates
North China Power Grid. It supplies power to an area of 1.47 million square kilometers,
covering Beijing, Tianjin, Hebei, Shanxi and West Inner Monogolia.
2.    Like most state-owned enterprises, NCPGC is faced with the following problems:
(a) government interference in management, administrative and operational decisions,
reflecting the former central planning orientation of the economy; (b) lack of full
accountability of managers stemming from an inadequate, highly centralized decision-
making and nonavailability of timely and accurate financial information at different
operational activity levels; (c) lack of transparency of the financial situation: financial
statements that are now prepared based on the new accounting regulation effective July 1,
1993 still do not provide full disclosure of NCPGC's financial position as the
construction in progress is recorded separately; and (d) lack of focus on the core business
operations and involvement in many activities that include profitable activities such as
construction companies, design/engineering institutes, as well as welfare responsibilities
such as housing, school, hospitals, etc.
3.    NCPGC is undertaking major changes to meet the operational challenges of
power sector reforms initiated by the Chinese Government. One of the main objectives
of these reforms is to establish a modem enterprise system characterized by clear
definition of property rights, autonomous management, commercial orientation, financial
independence, and separation of government ownership and regulatory functions from
enterprise management. To achieve these objectives, the Chinese Government and the
World Bank jointly developed an implementation program of sector reforms that stresses
full corporatization and greater autonomy and accountability of power enterprises. The
reform strategy is intended to improve the operational efficiency and increase the market
orientation of the power sector.
4.    NCPGC is expected to receive a loan from the World Bank to finance the
Tuoketuo Thermal Power Project. The project includes consultancy services to assist
NCPGC in upgrading its accounting and financial management practices and systems and
developing modern, computerized accounting and financial information systems, which
will enable managers to obtain timely information on the costs of all aspects of the
company's activities. The new systems would facilitate better budgetary control and



-71-                       ANNEX3.2
reporting on costs and finances to managers responsible for incurring expenditures and
also for external reporting to the Government, shareholders, lenders and the public.

- 79 -                     ANNEX 4.1
ANNEX 4.1: PROJECT DESCRIPTION: TUOKETUO
THERMAL POWER PLANT COMPONENT
General
1.    The owner of the project is Tuoketuo Electric Power Generating Company
(TEPGC). The domestic designer is the North China Electric Power Design Institute
(NCEPDI). Two coal-fired turbo-generating units of 600 MW each will be installed in
the plant to be financed under a proposed World Bank loan. The ultimate capacity of the
plant will be 3,600 MW (6 x 600 MW). The target date of the completion of the first
phase (2x600 MW) is September 2002. After completion of the project, the plant will
supply electric power to the Beijing-Tianjin-Tangshan area in North China.  The
scheduled dates of commercial operation of the two units are as follows:
Unit 1 - October 2001
Unit 2 - September 2002
2.    The proposed Tuoketuo thermal power plant is located in a plain in Tuoketuo
County, about 70 km south of Huhhot City, the capital of Inner Mongolia Autonomous
Region, about 50 km northeast of Zhungeer Coal Mine and 7 km north of the Yellow
River. It has favorable geological conditions and easy access by railway and highway.
The power plant will be leveled above the once-for- 100-year flood line.
Coal
3.    Basic design parameters for the boilers and turbine generators are based on standard
specifications of 600 MW coal-fired subcritical units of proven technology. The power
plant will use up to 4.0 million tons per year and will be designed to bum a blend of
screened unwashed coal from the Zhungeer coal mines. The coal will be bituminous with
a calorific value of 4,300+500 kcal/kg, ash content of 264 percent and sulfur content of
0.47 percent. The Zhungeer coal will be transported to the power station by trains, using
electric locomotives. The rolling stock will be owned by the power station, but the lines
are the property of the mine except for a spur of about 45 km to be built and owned by the
station.
Cooling and Make-upWater System
4.    The source of cooling and make-up water required by the power plant (1.2 m3/sec
in summer peak for the 2x600 MW units) will be supplied from the Yellow River. A
closed circulating water system will be adopted. Each unit will be equipped with one
cooling tower and three circulating water pumps.



- 80 -                        ANNEX 4.1
500 kV Transmission Lines and Associated Substations
5.    To transmit the electricity generated by the project to the JTTPG, three 500 kV
transmission lines and associated sub- and switching stations will be constructed under a
separate project that does not involve World Bank funding. One of these lines will run
from the Tuoketuo plant to the Anding substation in the suburbs of Beijing, a distance of
520 km. This line will pass through Yingxian, where a series capacitor compensation
station will be located. Another line, about 35 km in length, will connect the Tuoketuo
plant to the Yongshengyu switching station in Inner Mongolia. The third line (145 km)
will interconnect the Shunyi and Qianxi substations. The associated sub- and switching
stations include (a) the series capacitor compensation station in Yingxian; (b) the new
Yongshengyu switching station with three bays; (c) extension of the Anding substation
by one bay and installation of an additional 750 MVA transformer; and (d) the new
Qianxi substation in Beijing in which one 500 kV bay will be constructed and one
750 MVA transformer installed. The Shunyi-Qianxi line will also require an additional
bay in the Shunyi substation. Implementation of the transmission project will be
coordinated with the construction of the Tuoketuo generating station to ensure
completion of the new transmission infrastructure before trial operation of the generating
station begins. The total cost of the transmission lines and associated substations is
estimated to be Y 3,082 million (1995 prices), including compensation for land and
facilities acquisition. The environmental impact of these transmission lines is addressed
in Section 4.7 of the Tuoketuo environmental assessment report (EAR).
Turbines and Generators
6.    The two turbines will have a nominal rated output of 600 MW with subcritical'
steam pressure of 16.7 MPa at high-pressure turbine inlet and superheat and reheat
temperature of 538C each unit will be equipped with one high-pressure turbine bypass
system and one low-pressure turbine bypass system.
7.    The turbine generators will have a nominal capacity of 600 MW  each at 22 kV.
The cooling mode is a water-hydrogen-hydrogen type. A static excitation system will be
adopted.
For 600 MW class thermal power plants, there are two alternative configurations, one with subcritical
and the other with supercritical steam conditions. For the Tuoketuo project, the units will be designed
to have standard subcritical steam conditions because of the following reasons:
 The Tuoketuo power plant is a mine-mouth power plant. The subcritical plant is economically
justified because of relatively low fuel cost.
* The Tuoketuo power plant will be the first 600 MW class plant in the Inner Mongolia region.
(The largest existing plant in Inner Mongolia is the 330 MW Dalate power plant.) It is
premature to build a 600 MW supercritical unit in the Inner Mongolia Region.



- 81-                     ANNEX 4.1
Steam Generators
8.    The steam generators will be of the subcritical,' single reheat, dry bottom ash,
balanced draft, drum type, each rated to MCR of 2,020 tons/hour, steam pressure of
18.18 MPa and steam temperature of 5410C at superheater and reheater outlets. Each
steam generator will be equipped with six medium-speed mills. When burning "design
coal," five mills will be operated with one stand-by. Two boilers will share a 240 m
chimney.  For air pollution mitigation, the design includes four-field electrostatic
precipitator with 99.76 percent efficiency, low NOx burners and other low NOx
technology. Provision has been made for space to install gas desulfurization equipment,
if required in the future by more stringent environmental standards.
Coal Handling System
9.    Coal will be transported by railway from the Zhungeer coal mines to the power
plant with self-discharge bottom-dump cars and slope-type coal wagons. The project
includes a coal storage yard with a capacity of about 128,400 tons, which is equivalent to
10 days' coal consumption of the two 600 MW units.
Ash Handling System
10.   The two first 600 MW units, built under the proposed project, will produce about
1.13 million tons of fly ash and 0.22 million tons of slag each year. The ash yard will be
located 2 km south of the plant and will have the capacity corresponding to ash and slag
disposal for 17 years. To facilitate the utilization of fly ash, the power plant will be
provided with coarse ash and fine ash storages. TEPGC plans to utilize about 30 percent
of the fly ash. The fly ash from the electrostatic precipitators and the bottom of
economizers of the two units will be conveyed pneumatically to a dry ash silo where the
dry ash will be moisturized to ease its handling and piling in the ash yard. Slag will be
crushed and sluiced hydraulically in intermittent cycles into the front basin of the ash and
slag pumphouse. The ash and slag will be transferred hydraulically by the ash/slag
pumps to the ash yard. A recirculation water system will be adopted to reduce water
consumption. The cooling tower blowdown water of 600 tons/hour is supplied to the
system to compensate the evaporation from the ash yard of 600 tons/hour.
Instrumentation and Control System
11.   A microprocessor-based distributed control system including data acquisition
system (DAS), supervisory control system (SCS), control coordination system (CCS),
furnace fire fighting system (FSSS), etc. will be provided. Display of plant-specific
equipment status and operating parameters on CRTs installed in the central control room
will provide real-time interface between operators and plant systems.  On-line
performance monitoring system will be provided to increase plant performance, reduce
coal consumption and gradually introduce innovative advanced maintenance techniques.



- 82 -                    ANNEX4.2
ANNEX 4.2: PROJECT DESCRIPTION: BEIJING
TRANSMISSION AND DISTRIBUTION (T&D) COMPONENT
General
1.    Beijing T&D component is one of the two major components of the Tuoketuo
Thermal Power Project. The objective of the component is to reduce the constraints to
efficient transmission and distribution of power within the city of Beijing, particularly in
the densely populated, high load-growth areas around the city center.
2.   Investment in the transmission and distribution networks in Beijing over the last
decade have not kept pace with the increase in consumer demand. The Beijing Municipal
Electric Power Grid is therefore experiencing major operational problems: reduced
reliability of supply, overload of a number of major substations and lines, and high losses
in the system, especially in the city center. To ensure adequate supplies, it is necessary to
introduce more injection points at higher transmission voltages closer to the city center
and to upgrade the heavily loaded distribution system. These measures will improve
supply reliability, reduce losses and improve the quality of consumer service. The
component will achieve these objectives by providing new substations, installing reactive
compensation, increasing transformer capacities in substations and on distribution lines,
installing more efficient distribution transformers and increasing the sizes of conductors
on many distribution lines. These investments are needed to ensure that the power which
is to be transmitted from the Tuoketuo power station to Beijing can be efficiently relayed
to end-users while conforming to accepted standards of quality.
3.    The proposed component consists of the following items:
220 kV Indoor Substations
4.    Two new indoor substations will be constructed at Xibianmen and Xizhimen, two
areas in which the power demand is increasing rapidly. Xibianmen substation is to be
equipped with two 250 MVA, 220/110/10 kV transformers, two 30 MVAR capacitor
banks and gas-insulated switchgear (GIS). Xizhimen substation is proposed to have the
same configuration as Xibianmen but with two 200 MVA, 220/110/10 kV transformers.
Each substation will supply a number of 110/10 kV substations, which are not included in
the component but are either already existing or under construction. In addition, a
number of 10 kV feeders will emanate directly from the proposed substations. The
following element are also associated with the two new substations:
* 220 kV single-core XLPE cable (87.2 km)
*  110 kV single-core XLPE cable (1.1 km)



- 83 -                    ANNEX 4.2
* 10 kV switchgear (2 sets, 77 cubicles and 87 cubicles)
* Automatic transformer fire-extinguishing systems (2 sets)
* High-voltage protection equipment and substation supervisory and control
systems
5.    One 250 MVA, 220/110/10 kV transformer is to be installed in the Wangfujing
substation. This is an underground substation currently being constructed with two
250 MVA transformers. An additional transformer is required to efficiently satisfy the
rapidly increasing consumer demand. The proposed component therefore includes the
third transformer as well as the associated supply cables. In connection with and to
complement this project, NCPGC will undertake the following program, approved
separately and financed locally.
110/10 kV Transformers
6.    Four 50 MVA, 110/10 kV transformers will be installed to replace the overloaded,
inefficient transformers now installed in the Beicheng and Huichengmen substations.
The two substations were loaded at 104 percent and 98 percent of their respective rated
capacity in 1995. The existing transformers do not comply with statutory environmental
regulations concerning permissible noise levels, and the power utility must pay
appreciable amounts annually in penalties for not complying with the regulations.
Distribution Rehabilitation
7.    A pilot area of distribution system rehabilitation has been selected at Xizhimen
2
district located in the northwest of the city and covers an area of 8.3 km . The area is
densely populated and the power demand has been increasing rapidly. By the end of
1995, the area had a population of 220,000 and a peak demand of 40 MW. In order to
reduce the distribution losses and to improve the supply efficiency, the proposed
investments include:
  replacing the existing 41 km of 10 kV bare-conductor overhead line by three-
phase insulated conductor with larger cross-sections.
*  reconductoring of 32 km low-voltage lines
*  installation of five compact transformer stations with low-loss transformers
(6,300 kVA)
*  installation of 55 low-loss distribution transformers (16,025 kVA)
*  installation of 128 sets of capacitors
*  installation of 45 sets of distribution automation equipment
*  reconductoring of low-voltage lines to 8,905 residential consumers.
8.    The beneficiary of the component will be the North China Power Group Company
(NCPGC), which has responsibility for electricity transmission and distribution in
Beijing, through the Beijing Power Supply Company (BPSC). BPSC is an administrative
unit of NCPGC and not a legal entity in itself. NCPGC is also responsible for execution
of the component including construction, commissioning and operation. Beijing Power



- 84 -                    ANNEX 4.2
Supply Design Institute (BPSDI) will undertake preparation of technical bidding
document, bids evaluation, detailed construction design and supply of drawings for
Xizhimen and Wangfujing substations. North China Electric Power Design Institute
(NCEPDI) will be responsible for design of Xibianmen substation. The pilot project of
distribution rehabilitation will be completed in December 1998. Completion of erection
and testing of substation equipment is expected in March 1999 for Wangfujing, June
1999 for Xizhimen and August 1999 for Xibianmen. Commercial operation is also
scheduled in March 1999, June 1999 and August 1999, respectively, for the three
substations. The implementation of the entire component will be completed in August
1999.

ANNEX 4.3: TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR ENGINEERING
AND CONSTRUCTION MANAGEMENT SERVICES
Project Description
1.    The site of Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant is located on a plain in Tuoketuo
County, about 70 km south of Huhhot City, the capital of Inner Mongolia Autonomous
region, about 50 km northeast of Zhungeer Coal Mine and 7 km north of the Yellow
River. It has favorable geological conditions and easy access by railway and highway.
The owner of the project is Tuoketuo Electric Power Generating Company (TEPGC).
The domestic designer is the North China Electric Power Design Institute (NCEPDI).
The contractors for construction of civil works and plant installation will be selected
through local competitive bidding. Two coal-fired turbo-generating units of 600 MW
each will be installed in the plant to be financed under a proposed World Bank loan. The
ultimate capacity of the plant will be 3,600 MW (6 x 600 MW). The target dates of the
project completion are July 2001 and September 2002 for its first and second units,
respectively. After completion of the project, the plant will supply electric power to the
Beijing-Tianjin-Tangshan area.
2.    The contents of the project are listed below:  Two coal-fired steam turbo-
generating units each having a nameplate rating of 600 MW, complete with all electric
and mechanical accessories and auxiliaries as well as control equipment.
(a)   Coal handling and storage facilities.
(b)   Ash disposal facilities.
(c)   500 kV step-up substation.
(d)   Cooling water intake and discharge facilities, fresh water supply and water
treatment system.
(e)   All associated buildings and structures.
3.    The owner will be responsible for the preparation of bidding documents for all
plant equipment with the assistance from NCEPDI and a local consulting firm. It is
intended to engage foreign consulting engineers to provide consulting services listed in
paras. 5 to 22.



- 86 -                    ANNEX4.3
Procurement Arrangement
4.    The plant equipment is tentatively divided into four islands: boiler and auxiliaries
island (BI, including bottom ash disposal system), turbine-generator and auxiliaries island
(TGI, including plant electrical equipment), instrumentation and control island (I&CI)
and balance of plant island (BOPI). The BI, TGI, I&CI and a part of equipment in BOPI
as well as some other equipment and materials needed, such as simulator, environmental
monitoring equipment, communication facilities and construction materials will be
procured through international competitive bidding (ICB), limited international bidding
(LIB) and international shopping (IS) in accordance with the World Bank's Procurement
Guidelines (1995 version). Most of equipment in BOP island, civil works and plant
erection work will be procured locally by local financing.
Scope of Consulting Services to be Provided by Foreign Consulting Engineers
5.    Consulting services for this project will be carried out in three stages:
(a)   Stage 1: Review of bidding documents, review of bid evaluation and
assistance to contract negotiations.
(b)   Stage 2: Engineering and design interface coordination, vendor drawing
review, attendance at design liaison meetings and training for construction
management
(c)   Stage 3: Construction management
(Note: Services for Stage 1 and Stage 2 will be included in one contract. Services for
Stage 3 will be included in another separate contract that will be signed after the loan
agreement has been entered into force.)
Stage 1: Assistance in Review of Bidding Documents, Bid Evaluation and Contract
Negotiation
6.    Task 1: Assistance in review of bidding documents and finalization of
bidding documents. Consultants shall review the bidding documents for Boiler Island,
TG Island and I&C Island and provide a list of interfaces among these islands and review
reports to the owner. In reviewing the bidding documents, consultants shall place special
emphasis on the following aspects:
(a)   technical parameters
(b)   codes and standards
(c)   scope of contracts and completeness of specifications
(d)   design criteria (including calculation methods and type of drawing)



- 87 -                      ANNEX 4.3
(e)    quality assurance
(f)    design, manufacturing and delivery schedules
(g)   interfaces among various islands
7.    The review of the interface aspects shall:
(a)   ensure that scope of supply and design responsibility split is clearly
defined in each bid package, especially in the areas of integrated system
operation, piping, floor elevations, cables, intermediate junction boxes,
cable trays and supports; the division of design responsibility shall be
clearly identified, easy to understand and shall make all interfacing
contractors responsible for the interfacing design;
(b)   verify that interface points are shown correctly and not in contradiction
with the bid specifications;
(c)   ensure consistency  between turbine-generator and boiler technical
parameters;
(d)   check capacity, sizing, and proposed location of common facilities to be
provided with the new units, such as auxiliary boiler, water treatment
system, compressed air system, service water system, portable water
supply system, fuel oil storage and transfer facilities, switchyard and
communication system; consultants shall also assist in setting up turbine
building floor elevation, heater bay and deaerator elevation and column
line arrangement;
(e)   check the interface between the tripper floor of the coal handling system
and the boiler island supply and other interfaces between the coal handing
control room and the control room in the power block; check that the coal
handling system is adequate for both units; and
(f)   review one-line diagrams and layout of the switchyard.
In the course of reviewing, consultant shall correct any faulty wording in English in the
bidding documents.
8.    Task 2. Attendance at the prebid meeting. The consulting firm shall send his
mechanical, electrical and I&C experts to China to attend the prebid meeting for boiler
island and TG island held by the owner for 5-7 days and assist the owner in answering the
questions raised by bidders during the prebid meeting.
9.    Task 3. Assistance to Owner in bid evaluation, preparing bid evaluation
report.  Copies of all technical bids will be submitted to the consulting firm's
headquarters at the same time they are submitted to the Owner. The Owner will prepare a



- 88 -                     ANNEX 4.3
bidders list consisting of three to four bidders for Consultants' in-depth evaluation.
Consultant shall conduct a preliminary review and prepare preliminary comments in its
home office, then send a team of technical personnel consisting of Project Engineer,
Mechanical Engineer, Electrical Engineer, I&C Engineer, Civil Engineer and Boiler/
Turbine-Generator experts to China for four weeks, duration to work with the Owner to
reach preliminary results of evaluation for Boiler Island and Turbine-Generator Island.
Consultant's team will attend the clarification meeting to be held by the Owner during the
bid evaluation period and assist in preparation of bid evaluation report for each island
respectively.
10.   In the course of bid evaluation, Consultant shall:
(a)   review and clarify questions and problems;
(b)   assist in technical review of bids;
(c)   prepare a list of questions that require clarification from bidders;
(d)   assist in negotiation for alteration, adjustment and in answering questions
on the contents of specifications;
(e)   discuss preliminary evaluation results with the Owner;
(f)   discuss resolution of questions and problems in the bids with the Owner
and bidders;
(g)   review the responses from bidders during bid evaluation;
(h)   assist the Owner to determine the ranking of the bidders; and
(i)   provide comments on the qualification and experience of main
subcontractors of vendors.
11.   After the Owner has submitted the bid evaluation reports to the World Bank, if the
Bank has any questions regarding the evaluation report, Consultant shall assist the Owner
in answering them to the satisfaction of the World Bank.
12.   Task 4. Assist in technical negotiation of contracts, review technical contract
document. After the World Bank has given its no-objection to the bid evaluation report,
Consultant shall prepare associated data in his home office and send a team consisting of
five to six engineers to China for four weeks' duration for Boiler and TG island to work
with the Owner in technical negotiation of contracts. During negotiation, Consultant
shall assure that interfaces among various islands are clearly defined and interface
parameters and criteria determined through negotiation to be further confirmed in contract
documents. Consultant shall make efforts to define the contents and schedule of the
required design information exchange among Vendors and the Owner's design engineers.



- 89 -                    ANNEX 4.3
Consultant shall also help to set up the project procedures of correspondence and drawing
numbering system.

Stage 2: Engineering and Design Interface Coordination, Vendor Drawing Review,
Attendance at design Liaison Meetings and Training for Construction Management

engineering scope of island Vendors.
In order to monitor and expedite schedules of interface, Consultant shall
coordinate the project schedules among island Vendors, so that interface
coordination would be performed in time and data are complete; there
should be no gaps and overlaps.
(b)   Each of the Vendors will provide a monthly report about the interfacing
condition. Consultant, based on the schedule of information exchange,
supervise, manage and expedite the Vendor to exchange design
information based on interfacing condition.
Consultant shall be responsible for review of equipment drawings
technical documents and calculations to coordinate the interfaces between
each island contractors and to resolve interface problems and potential
interference in design done by contractors.
Consultant shall examine the interfaces between Vendors' drawings, shall
quickly handle the comments from various vendors so as to ensure all
interface points be confirmed. Comments on Vendors' drawings shall be
directly forwarded to them and copies shall be sent back to the Owner and
NCEPDI.
(c)   Consultant shall direct the Vendors of Boiler Island and TG Island to
compose a uniform piping interface list, in which the size, wall thickness,
material requirements as well as the preparing sketch of welding ends will
be all listed.

ANNEX 4.4: FINANCIAL AND LEGAL ADVISORY SERVICES
FOR ASSET DIVESTITURE-TERMS OF REFERENCE
A. INTRODUCTION AND OBJECTIVES
1.    IMEPC is a large state-owned enterprise with 72 subsidiaries and fixed assets up
to Y billion in 1995. It employs more than 60,000 people. The company's core business
is in power, but it has interests in a variety of other commercial operations. It has an
installed power generation capacity of 2,240 MW composed of 15 thermal power plants,
with annual energy generated at 11.8 TWh. It was classified as one of 10 outstanding
enterprises that yield good profits and tax revenues in the primary industrial sector in
China.
2.    In 1994, IMEPC sold 11 TWh with a profit after tax of Y 245 million. In
addition, IMEPC made a profit of Y 30 million in construction and Y 48 million in other
business. The company has one power plant listed on the Shanghai Stock Exchange
Market, and plans to issue fresh equity for this facility. It has joint ventures with outside
investors to build power plants and transmit power to the Beijing area. The Tuoketuo
Electric Power Generating Company (TEPGC) in which IMEPC owns 35 percent of the
equity is one such example.
3.    IMEPC is currently embarking on a program to obtain additional financial
resources through asset sales, public equity listing and private investment. The main
elements of this program are:
(a)   Sale of Wulashan Power Plant. Wulashan power plant comprise units of
2x50 MW built in 1975 and lxlOO MW built in 1978. These units have an
excellent operating record and have received awards for efficient and
reliable operation. The assets have been revalued at Y 520 million. In
March 1996, the sales of these assets was approved by the Inner Mongolia
Authorities. These assets are expected to be sold to Sinochem by end-
1997. A limited liability company will be established to support the sale.
(b)   Listing of Inner Mongolia Mendian Huaneng Thermal Power Co.
(IMMHTPC). IMMHTPC is a shareholding company comprising
425 MW of generation and district heat supply. The company has a total
share capital of Y 412 million, of which Y 50 million or 12.14 percent is
listed in the Shanghai exchange. By mid-1997, additional shares are to be
offered in Shanghai. It is expected that Y 60 million would be raised
through this listing.



- 97 -                    ANNEX 4.4
(c)   Private participation in Haibowan Electric Power Co. (HEPC). HEPC
is a limited liability company comprising plants of 2x100 MW with an
additional 2x200 MW under construction. The registered capital of HEPC
is Y 500 million.
4.    The main objectives of this task is to assist IMEPC to:
(a)   undertake the corporate and financial restructuring to support the sale of
private equity in Haibowan Electric Power Company (HEPC);
(b)   develop the appropriate legal and contractual documentation; and
(c)   complete the private equity placement for the Haibowan Electric Power
Company (HEPC).
Scope and Organization of Work
5.    The principal client for this task will be IMEPC. However, as IMEPC is a state-
owned enterprise whose decisions are subject to the approval of provincial government
agencies, the Consultant will hold discussions with these agencies as appropriate. The
Consultant's main tasks are as follows:
Phase I: Diagnostic and Preparation
(a)   Review the proposals of IMEPC for the divestiture of existing thermal
stations. Financial models will be prepared and the viability of divestiture
examined under different scenarios.
(b)   Review and discuss the scope involvement of potential domestic and/or
foreign investors in the existing limited liability company and their
participation in the development of the second phase of the plant. The
objective here would be to develop the optimal mode of investor
involvement to provide additional capital future expansion of HEPC.
(c)   Undertake market soundings and review the expectations of domestic and
international investors on the sales of equity of HEPC and the
attractiveness of the assets from the market's perspective.
(d)   Develop clear proposals for the asset sales of HEPC.   Preliminary
valuation and financial modeling will be undertaken to determine the
viability the transaction.  The models will be further developed in
subsequent stages for the preparation of power sales agreements, and
private equity offering.



- 98 -                    ANNEX 4.4

6.    To solicit investors to participate in the private equity sales of HEPC it will be
necessary to prepare a complete package of legal and contractual documents. The
Consultant will prepare the following documentation:
(a)   Revision of Incorporation documents of HEPC with additional private
equity
*     Articles of Association
*     Legal incorporation
*     Opening balance sheets and financial accounts
(b)   Power Sales Agreements between HEPC and IMEPC. This would include:

etc.
(c)   Bidding documents and prospectus for the private equity sales to advance
the asset divestiture process. The Consultant will assist in developing the
appropriate bid evaluation criteria.
7.    The Consultant will assist IMEPC in all aspects of financial and corporate
restructuring, developing the above legal documents and the associated legal and
financial procedural requirements. The Consultant will ensure that all legal procedures
and documents are in accordance with Chinese Law and regulations.
Phase III: Completion of Private Equity Sales of HEPC
8.   In this phase, the Consultant will undertake all activities necessary for a
successful private equity sales of HEPC:
(a)   Preparing and conducting prebid conferences and roadshows.
(b)   Tendering and evaluation of bids.
(c)   Completion of the transaction with all necessary legal documentation.
Consultant Qualifications
9.    The Consultant will be a qualified consortium comprising:
* A reputed international financial advisory firm
* An international law firm, and
* A domestic Chinese law firm
10.   The Consultant will be selected by the Client with the assistance of the World
Bank. The following criteria will guide the selection of the Consultant:



-99-                       ANNEX 4.4
(a)   Demonstrated experience in providing corporate, commercial, financial

ANNEX 4.5: ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT UNIT-
TERMS OF REFERENCE
INTRODUCTION
1.    The Tuoketuo Electric Power Generation limited liability Company (TEPGC) will
establish environmental management capabilities and include in its institutional structure
an environmental management unit (EMU).
2.    Technical assistance (TA) will be included in the project to establish
environmental capabilities within the new entity. TA will be provided in two stages:
(1) analyze institutional, professional and financial requirements for the EMU, in
accordance with the objectives outlined below, and (2) assist initial EMU operation. TA
is to include: (1) assistance in creating environmental functions within the EMU,
(2) development of corporate policies and regulations based upon China's requirements,
(3) establish corporate standards in operations, engineering and safety, (4) establish
monitoring capabilities, (5) establish guidelines for environmental auditing, and
environmental impact assessment (EIA), (6) create infrastructure for rehabilitation of
oustees, (7) develop resettlement and rehabilitation (R&R) budgeting and norms,
(8) establish laboratories, (9) human resources development, and (10) design and
operationalize a environmental data management system.
Current Status of IMEPA Environmental Institutional Capability
3.   IMEPA has a limited number of environmental staff.  There is limited
institutional capability for environmental monitoring and data analysis, and management
of worker health and safety issues. Most monitoring is performed by Inner Mongolia
Enviromnental Protection Bureau.
Objectives
4.    Objectives of the TA will be to assist the newly formed entity to achieve the
following capabilities at both corporate and field levels:
(a)   Overall
(i)    Develop environmental management capabilities. Establish and
environmental management unit (EMU) at corporate headquarters,
and an EMU at the Tuoketuo power station
(ii)   Enhance computer data base, environmental modeling capabilities,
GIS mapping capabilities, and office technology for the EMUs



-101-                      ANNEX4.5
(iii)   Improve capabilities to produce quality Environmental Impact
Assessments (EIAs)
(b)   Technical
(i)    Develop environmental policies,
(ii)   Standardize  effluent  and  emissions  disposal,  treatment
technologies, soil stabilization techniques, and preservation of flora
and fauna
(iii)   Establish  corporate  training  programs  to  track  changing
environmental regulations for environment and health and safety
staff at both corporate and field levels
(iv)    Coordinate and control environmental compliance and safety
performance of plants and installations. Conduct trend analysis
and prepare exception reports
(v)    Enhance environmental data collection and analysis capabilities
(c)   Resettlement and Rehabilitation (R&R)
(i)   Establish a R&R unit to manage all aspects of land acquisition,
community development, planning implementation and monitoring
(ii)    Develop company R&R policies
(iii)   Strengthen human resources development programs
(iv)   Improve quality of life in employee colonies
Technical Activities
5.    The Corporate level EMU will engage in the following activities when fully
developed:
(a)   Policies and regulations:
(i)   Formulate operational guidelines to conform  with China's
environmental standards, laws and regulations
(ii)    Develop  corporate targets for pollution  prevention, waste
reduction, soil conservation, and water resources protection
(iii)    Develop  energy  conservation  programs  for  generation,
transmission and demand side management

Implementation
11.   Prior to initiating technical assistance, management of the newly formed entity
will appoint a Director for the Corporate EMU who will then work with the Technical
Assistance team to determine precise needs for development of environmental staff at
both corporate and field levels.
12.  It is expected that the Director of the Corporate EMU will be an Executive
Director with exclusive responsibility for environment, and worker safety and health.
Interim Procedures
13.   During the initial study phase, a temporary environment cell will form the nucleus
of the fully developed EMI which will eventually evolve. Objectives for this cell are as
follows: (1) form a counterpart team to the Consultant, (2) handle routine environmental
affairs.
14.   Requirements for the environmental team are as follows:
(a)   Environmental Technical Unit would be responsible for policies and
regulations, standardization of effluent and emission control technologies,
assure vigilance regarding compliance with environmental regulations.
Anticipated skills for this group include expertise in:  wastewater
management, soil and water resources protection, air pollution
management, ecology, EIA and environmental audit preparation
(b)   Resettlement and Rehabilitation Unit would be responsible for R&R
policies, and human resource development
(c)   Training Unit will be responsible for organizing and administering safety,
R&R, and environmental training programs
(d)   Monitoring and Data Management Unit will be responsible for
monitoring effluents, and emission, air and water quality and another other
environmental parameters stipulated by China, IMEPB, or HEPB or local
authorities.   The unit will also establish computer data bases,
environmental modeling and office technology equipment for the
environmental units
(e)   Safety Unit will be responsible for firefighting, and emergency
contingency plans, worker health and safety, safety audits and standards,
monitoring and inspection.



-105 -                      ANNEX 4.6
ANNEX 4.6: CONSULTANCY SERVICES FOR
ESTABLISHING AND OPERATIONALIZING THE
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT UNIT (EMU)-TERMS
OF REFERENCE
Introduction
1.    The Autonomous Region of Inner Mongolia contains vast coal reserves whose
development will be dramatically expanded in the near future. Consistent with this
increase in coal production will be the substantial development of power generation
facilities in this region on a scale heretofore never experienced. Tuoketuo Electric Power
Generation limited liability Company (TEPGC) recognized the need and priority for
addressing environmental and social issues in planning and implementing this
development.  Consequently, it is their intention to establish an environmental
management unit (EMU) within their corporate structure to insure proper attention is
given to these matters in terms of both immediate management, and their strategic
planning. TORs for this EMU are attached.
2.    In addition to TEPGC's efforts to incorporate the environmental and social
dimension to their development activities, local and regional environmental authorities
also play key roles, particularly with regard to air and water quality management. Air
quality was identified as a priority issue. These authorities wish technical assistance to
provide them with the necessary tools to prepare an quality management plan.
Objectives
3.    The objectives of this work effort are as follows:
* Design a detailed work program for the EMU
* Support initial startup and operation of the EMU
* Design a detailed training program in air quality management
4.    A description of the Consultant' work program is presented below.
DEVELOPMENT OF THE EMU WORK PROGRAM
5.    The Consultant will prepare a Work Program for the EMU for the next three
years. Prior to the preparation of this program, the Consultant will review: (a) the
Chinese regulatory framework (state, provincial and local) for pollution control and social
assessment, and (b) regional power sector development plans. The Consultant will then
Consultant is to be considered local unless otherwise noted.



- 106 -                      ANNEX 4.6
hold discussions with appropriate government officials, and based on these discussions
identify key environmental and social issues associated with the development of power
generation capacity in the region.
6.    This Task will be the basis on which to identify the priority objectives and
activities of the EMU Work Program. Priority objectives should be developed for
implementation at both corporate and power station or field installation. For each set of
objectives, the Consultant should define specific performance criteria for each activity at
corporate and field levels.
7.    A staffing plan should be prepared by the Consultant in collaboration with staff of
TEPGC. This plan should incorporate both requirements for hiring new permanent staff,
reassignment of current staff, and utilizing consultants (local or foreign) for some of the
activities.
8.    The foreign Consultant will than prepare a training program consistent with the
staffing plan. This program will include identification of: necessary skills needed by the
EMU staff, appropriate trainers, and/or training programs (both domestic and
international). Visits to China by international experts, overseas travel by company
personnel for specific training programs are some of the possible options. Training
programs should include, but not be limited to the following subject areas: environment
and natural resources management, pollution control (air, water, solids), resettlement,
rehabilitation and community development, environmental monitoring, data collection
and processing, EIA preparation, environmental and safety audits, interpretation and
implementation of environmental regulations, and computer system design for
environmental management.
9.    The training program will include a curriculum for the various subjects, and a
estimate of classroom, and training aids needed. It should also include a mobilization
plan for the trainers, equipment, and facilities, to be utilized from within the company,
within China, or imported internationally.
10.   The foreign Consultant should also prepare a detailed financial plan for the
training program. The plan should identify costs (local/foreign) of international trainers,
overseas training by TEPGC staff, equipment and training aids (books, literature, tapes,
videos, etc.).
POLICY GUIDELINES AND REGULATIONS
11.   The consultant will prepare draft policy guidelines and regulations consistent with
the objectives as specified in the TORs of the EMU (attached). In particular:
* Guidelines and interpretation of China's laws and regulations that will enable
the company to comply in a timely and cost-effective manner. Corporate
targets for atmospheric emissions of dust, sulfur dioxide, and nitrogen oxides,
wastewater effluent discharges, solid wastes (particularly ash, and spent



- 107 -                    ANNEX 4.6
sorbents from sulfur dioxide abatement systems), and worker health and
safety.
Targets will be established on the basis of anticipated future framework of
environmental regulation in China, international treaties/agreements, and
corporate development plans. The targets will depend on options in fuel
quality, abatement technology, and an assessment of potential for energy
conservation (demand side).
*  Guidelines for EIA preparation, identifying key issues, and requirements of
China, and multilateral institutions (World Bank, Asian Development Bank,
etc.).
*  Guidelines for resettlement and rehabilitation of peoples affected by corporate
projects.
*  Establish guidelines for the utilization, preservation and management of
natural resources (air, water, land, forests, cultural, etc.).
*  Guidelines for worker and workplace health and safety.
Technical/Operational and Management Guidelines
12.   The Consultant will prepare a set of operational standards, performance criteria,
good practice, and procedures for the following:
*  Worker Health: the Consultant will review standards of China, and various
international organizations, and use these as a basis of his recommendations.
-  Worker Safety: the Consultant will review plant safety rating systems and,
based upon these systems, formulate one or more systems for use in various
field installations.
*  Emergency Response:   The Consultant will prepare guidelines for
formulating emergency response plans.
*  Environmental Monitoring  and  Data Management System:   The
Consultant will prepare a monitoring guideline package for power plants and
transmission systems, including methods, equipment selection criteria, data
processing and reporting. The package should also include atmospheric
dispersion models (guidelines for selection), and monitoring of ecological
impacts at power stations and along transmission lines, community and
occupational health. The package should also include criteria for the selection
of monitoring contractors, and standard TOR.
*  Auditing: The Consultant will prepare detailed TOR for power plant and
transmission line environmental audits. Auditing procedures should include
worker health and safety aspects as well as environment.



-108 -                     ANNEX 4.6
DESIGN OF A CORPORATE ENVIRONMENTAL LABORATORY
13.   The Consultant will prepare a detailed design of an environmental laboratory.
The design should include personnel requirements (number of staff and skills) sampling
and analysis equipment requirements (stationary and mobile), and complete itemization
of expendables (glassware, chemicals, etc.) to keep the laboratory operating for three
years.
DESIGN AND IMPLEMENTATION OF AN ENVIRONMENTAL DATA MANAGEMENT SYSTEM
14.   The foreign Consultant will review the environmental monitoring program for the
Tuoketuo thermal power station. Based upon this review, and the various environmental
monitoring requirements of China, IMEPB, HEPB and TEPB, the foreign Consultant will
establish the quantity and quality (electronically or manually recorded, etc.) of
environmental data to be received.
15.   Based upon this information, the foreign Consultant will design a computer-based
data collection and analysis system, which will include both hardware and software
requirements and design specifications. The design is to include system costs.
16.   After agreement is reached with EMU management on the environmental data
management system design, the foreign Consultant will assist the EMU in securing and
installing the equipment, and operationalizing the system.
17.   The system should be capable of generating environmental data reports to meet
the needs of TEPGC management, China's environmental authorities (NEPA), and both
the provincial and local environmental protection bureaus (IMEPB, TEPB). Furthermore,
the system design should be "expandable," in the sense that it can be readily adapted to
the additional environmental data that will be generated when the second, and third
phases of Tuoketuo are on line.
SUPPORT AND SERVICE: DESIGN OF AN AIR QUALITY MANAGEMENT TRAINING
PROGRAM
18.   Local environmental officials are responsible for preparation of an air quality
management plan for the Tuoketuo area. Such a plan has not yet been prepared, nor do
the officials involved have the technical experience needed to produce this plan.
However, these officials wish to receive the necessary training in air quality management
to be able to accomplish this task.
19.   The foreign Consultant will design a technical training program for officials of the
local environmental protection bureaus, in the area of air quality management planning.
The training is to be designed so that trainees will subsequently be able to prepare an air
quality management plan for the Tuoketuo region.

below:

and analysis shall be prepared in both in computer-accessible software (disk) and hard
copy. Copies of software with associated user manuals will also be supplied to the
company, and training in their use is to be provided on completion of the study.
25.   Direct and indirect costs associated with training the staff, exclusive of the time
dedicated by the Consultant in establishing and operationalizing the EMU, will be borne

-111-                       ANNEX 4.7
ANNEX 4.7: ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PROGRAM
A. SUMMARY OF KEY PROJECT ENVIRONMENTAL ISSUES
Air Pollution
1.    Table 1 presents air pollution characteristics for the proposed project (1200 MW),
and the total power program planned for the site (3600 MW). As can be seen, emission
standards for dust, sulfur dioxide, and nitrogen oxides are all in compliance with Chinese
standards and World Bank guidelines. Air quality data are also presented, and for both
sulfur dioxide, and nitrogen oxides, it is predicted that the project (1200 MW) and overall
program (3600 MW) will not result in a violation of World Bank guidelines and most
Chinese standards.) Existing background dust levels exceed both Chinese standards, and
World Bank guidelines. This is not unusual for China in general, and in particular for
this area which is close to desert conditions. With project implementation, and ultimately
with the overall program, these dust levels have been estimated to be slightly elevated.
However, the estimated increases are so small as to be virtually undetectable if they were
real, and well within the error bounds of the model.
2.    Carbon dioxide emissions are estimated to be 0.0067 and 0.020 billion tons/year
for the 1,200 MW and 3,600 MW situations, respectively. This represents 0.031 and
0.093 percent of the annual industrial global burden.
3.    Finally, estimates of the Tuoketuo power program (3,600 MW) contribution to the
acid rain/acid deposition issues in China were estimated using the RAINS-ASIA model
developed in ASTEN. Results of these calculations indicated that the levels of acid
deposition are relatively low.
The "once maximum" for sulfur dioxide is estimated to exceed the Chinese standard by 3 percent when
the program is fully implemented (3,600 MW). For the proposed project (1,200 MW), no exceedance
occurs. Even in the case of the full 3,600 MW program, the small exceedance is well within the errors
of air quality modeling and monitoring.

Water Pollution
4.       The power station will recycle wastewaters to the greatest extent possible.  Any
excess wastewater will be discharged after appropriate treatment to meet Chinese
standards and World Bank guidelines. Treatment, when needed, will be either physical
and/or biological. Most of the cooling tower blowdown will be reused. A breakdown of
water reuse characteristics is presented below:

6.     Impacts to water quality of the Yellow River from the effluent discharge were
estimated. From Table 3 presented below, it is seen that beyond the mixing zone in the
most critical situations (low flow, and average flow) water quality meets Chinese water
quality standards. Furthermore, the shape of the mixing zone does not traverse the entire
river width, so that mobile species can simply avoid the zone by swimming away.
Therefore, it is unlikely that the effluent will present any negative impact on aquatic
ecology of the Yellow River.

-114 -                      ANNEX 4.7
Coal Transport and Handling
7.    Fuel to the Tuoketuo power station will be low-sulfur bituminous coal obtained
from the Zhungeer Coal Mine. The mine is located approximately 44 km from the power
station. At the mine location a new, large coal-washing plant has been constructed, but is
not yet operational. The power station fuel supply will be an unwashed, screened product
of this washing plant, containing 0.47 percent sulfur and 30.0 percent ash. The coal
(14,520 tons/day) will be shipped along the Zhungeer-Fengzhen dedicated rail line, which
is under Zhungeer Coal Industry Corporation control.
8.    At the coal storage yard, sprinkling facilities using a portion of the cooling tower
blowdown will be installed for dust suppression. Spraying will be done on a regular
basis. A rotary sprinkler system will be provided for dust suppression at loading and
unloading sections of the stacker reclaimer, belt conveyor, and feeder. A cyclone
separator will be used at each transfer station, coal bunker bay and in the crusher room.
Baghouses will be provided at coal storage silos. All excess runoff water shall be
collected, treated and recycled.
Ash Management
9.    Ash will be slurried with cooling water blowdown and pumped to the Gaobashi
ash yard. The ash yard is about 2 km south of the power station has sparse vegetation and
poor soil stability. Currently two households (four people) live at the site and they will
be resettled. For Phase 1 (1,200 MW), the site occupies 3.36 km2, will be constructed to
a height of 15 meters and its life is estimated at 17.3 years. When all three phases are
2
complete (3,600 MW), the site will be expanded to 6.36 km , will be filled to a height of
30 meters, and have an expected life of 24 years.
10.   Most of the site has a natural layer of clay to protect groundwater. However, there
are sufficient areas at the site that do not have this clay layer. Modeling studies indicated
that if the site were to be used without an additional impermeable liner, the groundwater
would become polluted. There are four potable wells within 500-1,000 m of the site, so
protection of this groundwater is required. Based upon these factors, a sufficient layer of
clay will be added at those points at the disposal area where there is no naturally
occurring clay. Then, a geotextile liner, 3-4 mm thick, will be used over the entire ash
disposal site to protect groundwater.  Potable wells will be monitored regularly
throughout the project life, and additional monitoring wells will be drilled at the site
periphery to further ensure against contamination.
11.   To prevent dusting, the area will be covered with water. A sprinkling system
utilizing recirculated cooling tower blowdown is included as a protective measure, should
any localized "dry spots" occur at the ash yard. Water drains underneath the ash yard will
collect water and recycle it with the ash slurry system. The ash yard will be partitioned
into cells, each representing about 10 percent of the total surface area. Cells will be used
one at a time. Each cell will be filled and covered before the next one is used. This will



-115 -                      ANNEX 4.7
further minimize dust formation and ensure adequate water is available to wet the ash
suffice in the driest periods of the year.
12.   A 100 meter band of forest will be planted around the yard, to act as a windbreak
and remove the site from view. When the ash yard is filled, it will be covered with soil
and revegetated in a manner consistent with principles of dryland vegetation.
Transmission Line and Distribution System
13.   The 500 kV line will deliver power to Beijing a distance of approximately
507 km. The line will travel over rugged mountainous terrain as well as farmland, and
cross eight rivers (none navigable), through the Provinces of Inner Mongolia, Shanxi, and
Hebei. There will be no resettlement involved, and no historic or protected areas (local or
State) are traversed. The closest site along the route is the Heng Mountain scenic spot,
32 km from the power line.
14.   There are no migratory bird routes crossing the transmission lines, so no
protective measures will be used on the transmission towers to prevent bird electrocution.
It is estimated that about 40 km2 of land will be occupied by the transmission towers.
Tower design will be in accordance with all Chinese standards with respect to noise and
electric field.
15.   Within the Xizhimen region of Beijing, a distribution component will replace
some lines in the distribution network as well as some existing transformers with five
compact transformer stations.  No impacts are expected from  these replacement/
rehabilitation activities. No PCBs will be used in the transformers or capacitors, and this
will be so specified in the bid documents. Transformers that are to be replaced do not
contain PCBs and written assurances have been provided by responsible authorities
confirming this fact.
Railway
16.   Coal will be transported along a dedicated rail line from coal-washing plant to
power station. The railroad will be located along the eastern bank of the Yellow River.
The route passes through both rugged mountainous terrain and flat farming areas. Special
attention will be paid to construction techniques, particularly in the mountainous region,
to avoid modifications to runoff patterns. The rail will be designed to minimize noise
when trains are in use. The track will occupy approximately 260.2 ha but no resettlement
will be required.
17.   There are four stations along the route. Two of these stations, Wang Yu Ying and
Lan Jia Yao, will generate a total of 37 m3/day of wastewater, which will be skimmed for
removal of oil (0.647 kg/day). Treated wastewater will be used for irrigation, and
collected oil will be given to employees for use as cooking oil.



-116-                        ANNEX 4.7
Water Supply
18.   The water source for the power plant will be the Yellow River. For Phase I,
approximately 1.0 m3/sec will be required. There are three basic components to the water
supply system: intake structure, treatment (clarification/settling pond), and delivery
pipeline to the power station. Location of the intake structure is approximately 12 km
southwest of the plant site. Of the total water withdrawn, the portion of water to be used
for cooling tower makeup will be chlorinated.
19.   The river bank will be stabilized to protect the intake structure. This will have the
added benefit of stabilizing the river course, preventing erosion, and protecting both the
people and property in the vicinity. Impacts on navigation at the location of the intake
structure were estimated to be negligible.
20.   The chief potential impact will be dust generated at the area to be established for
disposition of silt which will be removed from the settling pond. A 71.3 ha site is to be
established for this purpose. It will be filled to a height of 3.4 meters. In order to
minimize dust generation, silt will be conditioned to make it easy to vegetate and then the
area will be reclaimed with appropriate plants. A windbreak will also be planted on the
periphery to lower wind velocity, and thereby further reduce dust generation potential.
Noise
21.   The power station is to be located in a sparsely populated area. There are no
major communities, or human activities within the vicinity proposed for the plant.
Nonetheless, the plant will be designed so that all equipment will meet the appropriate
standards of maximum allowable noise generation (GB 12348-90: Noise Standard at
Boundaries of Industries and Enterprises). These requirements will be specified in the
equipment bid documents.
22.   An analysis of noise potential indicated the following sources were most
significant: turbine generator set, coal mill, cooling tower, and transformer section. The
analysis further indicated that to ensure noise standards will be met in the community,
silencers are to be used for the boiler safety valves, and boiler exhaust. The plant
enclosure will be sound-proofed to contain noise generated by the turbine, coal grinding
units, etc.
23.   Chinese noise standards are more stringent than those of the World Bank. Thus,
compliance with Chinese standards offers implicit compliance with World Bank
Environmental Guidelines.
Aquatic/Terrestrial Ecology
24.   The project will be located in a relatively uninhabited area that is classified as dry
semi-arid grassland. Forest growth in the area is poor and it is considered to be of low
botanical diversity and difficult to afforest. The quantity of aquatic species in the Yellow



-117 -                      ANNEX 4.7
River are considered to be low production. There are no rare or endangered species, and
few animal species inhabiting the site.
25.   During construction, there will be some disruption (temporary and permanent) to
both wildlife habitat and vegetative cover. However, appropriate construction techniques
should minimize any impacts. A large soil conservation/desertification control program
is included in the project, which will more than compensate for any loss of vegetative
cover.
26.   Air quality impacts to agriculture and vegetation from sulfur dioxide (SO2) and
fluoride (F-) were estimated to be negligible. Ash pond runoff waters will be collected
and managed, and all wastewaters will be treated to standards prior to discharge.
Therefore no impacts on the aquatic ecology are anticipated.
Occupational Health and Safety
27.   Appropriate considerations will be incorporated into the design and operation of
the plant and related facilities to insure worker health and safety. Special considerations
were incorporated into the design to assure safe conditions in the management of
hazardous materials (fuel oil, chlorine, hydrogen, caustic, etc.). International standards of
worker safety will be included in all bid documents of project equipment. Boilers, and
other potentially dangerous equipment will be designed to meet ASME standards of
safety and will be so specified in the bid documents. Polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs)
are illegal in China; their use is prohibited in the project. Prohibition of asbestos will be
specified in the bid documents.
Human Environment
28.   There are no important tourism resources in the Tuoketuo area. No sites of
archaeological, historic, religious, architectural or aesthetic value recognized by the State
or the autonomous region are located at the project area. The nearest cultural landmarks
are in the capital city of Hohhot.
29.   From June 20 to June 22, 1994, public meetings were held at Xikoukou village of
Yanshanying county. General conclusions of the participants were:
*  Tuoketuo project is beneficial to both country and local people
*  The project will not cause environmental pollution, but rather improve the
local standard of living
*  Relocation arrangements were satisfactory
*  The project will improve the local economy

ANNEX 4.8: DESERTIFICATION CONTROL COMPONENT
Introduction
1.    The Tuoketuo thermal power plant (2x600 MW) is located in a region where soil
erosion and land desertification causes an increasing concern. As part of the project, a
desertification control component has been designed and will be implemented in order to
mitigate the adverse environmental impacts of the power plant and to contribute to
improving the conditions and standards of living of the population in the project area
(about 46,000 people).
Scope of the Component
2.    The component consists of two parts:
(a)   Part A: intensive afforestation of the areas immediately surrounding the
power plant, ash disposal yard, cooling water intake, water supply and
discharge pipelines, and access roads.
(b)   Part B: selective afforestation of the region around the Tuoketuo power
plant, covering a total surface area of 400 km2 (20 km x 20 km)
concerming two counties and one minority banner (equivalent to county).
3.    The total afforested area upon completion of this component will be 3,137 ha
(4,535,000 trees), in which Part A involves 120 ha (228,000 trees). An illustration map
(IBRD 28283) is attached. The major activities of the component comprise:
(a)   afforestation by manual planting and aerial seeding,
(b)   introduction of high-wind and drought-resistant tree species to the existing
sparse and low-yield forestry,
(c)   construction of a nursery to provide seedlings,
(d)   dissemination of new technologies of afforestation to local people, and
(e)   landscaping around the power plant.
4.    The equipment and facilities in association with this component include motor-
pumped wells and canals for irrigation, planting equipment, vehicles, access roads, tool
warehouse, power supply and communication facilities.



-125 -                      ANNEX 4.8
Cost Estimate and Financing Plan
5.    The investment cost of the component is estimated at Y 9.05 million (about $1.09
million), of which the Part A related cost is Y 2.49 million. Details are shown in Table 1.
