1997    1998   1999   2000    2001
Y'000           1,518.4  1,830.1  2,333.0  2,323.8  1,046.1
7.    The component will be financed by TEPGC, central government and local
government. TEPGC will meet the entire cost of Part A and contribute 25 percent of the
cost of Part B, which together will amount to Y 4.18 million. The balance will be
covered by government funds, of which 30 percent by the Ministry of Forestry and 70
percent by Hohhot municipality and Tuoketuo county.
Implementation Aspect
8.    A unit in charge of implementation of this component will be set up within the
organization of TEPGC. The unit will have 11 permanent employees. Temporary
workers will be contracted as required. The unit will work closely with the local
government and people. Since the purpose and activities of the component comply with
that of three state-sponsored programs, known as "Three-North Shelter Forest Program,"
"Nationwide Afforestation Program" and "Nationwide Sand Prevention and Control
Program," it is expected that strong supports will be given by the govermnent at different
levels in implementing the component.



-126 -                       ANNEX 4.8
9.    The feasibility study of this component was carried out by the Inner Mongolia
Forestry Science Academy, which is experienced in desertification control. The selected
species are best suited to local environment conditions, and high pollution resistant. They
also yield high economic value. Locally available species will be widely used. The
designed multifunction forests are for timber, road shelter, farm field shelter, sand control
shelter, soil conservation and cash-tree. The year-to-year afforestation plan is given
below:
1997     1998      1999      2000      2001
Total (ha)          254.61    1,180.12    723.63   723.63    250.61
in which Part A (ha)  11.97    23.94     35.90     35.90      11.97
Economic Cost/Benefit Analysis
10.   All the costs and benefits are expressed in economic terms using shadow pricing.
The actual market rate is used as the shadow price for labor costs. Taxes are excluded.
The planning period is 20 years (1997-2016).
11.   The costs include investment costs and operating costs. The benefits of the
component stem from direct incomes, environmental and social benefits.
(a)    Direct incomes are from  selling forestry products, such as timber,
seedling, and fruits, and are measured by the market values.
(b)   Environmental benefit.  The implementation of the component can
protect the facilities of the power plant as well as 21 km railway and road
from soil and wind erosion. It will protect 3,578 ha of agricultural land.
Protection of agricultural land from soil and wind erosion are counted as
indirect benefits, which are measured using the standard issued by the
"Three-North Shelter Forest Program." In addition, afforestation will
improve the air quality because trees are very effective in absorption of
S02 and CO2. It is also expected that a 10-15 dB reduction of noise level
will be achieved at the area of the power plant. However, these two items
are not included in the benefit calculation.
(c)    Social benefit. Construction and operation of a power plant on a scale of
1,200 MW in one of the poorest counties in China will create jobs and
generate incomes in the region, and thus greatly alleviate poverty
conditions in Tuoketuo county. However, only the afforestation program
directly related social benefits are discussed here. The component will
provide 11 permanent jobs (in the implementation unit) as well as 2,260
persons for short-term afforestation work. Local people will also benefit
from the new technologies introduced in developing high-wind and



-127-                           ANNEX4.8
drought-resistant forestry.   Social benefits are not included in the
calculation of benefits.
12.   The cash flows are presented in Table 2 and 3. An IERR of 20 percent is obtained
for the whole component and 30% for Part A.

- 129 -                    ANNEX 4.9
ANNEX 4.9: LAND ACQUISITION AND RELOCATION
General
1.    Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant and Beijing T&D are the two main components of
the project. Both components involve land acquisition, and relocation of population. The
resettlement for the former takes place in the rural area in Inner Mongolia and for the
latter in the urban area of Beijing. The priority was given to minimize the scope of
resettlement throughout the project design and planning. Where land acquisition and
demolition of existing housing are unavoidable, the resettlement plans provide for
replacement of housing, agricultural land, infrastructure, services and other resources.
The RAPs aim at improving the standards of living of the PAPs or at least to restoring
them.
2.    For Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant, the resettlement will be carried out in two
phases. The first phase includes resettlement activities related to the power plant site and
the ash disposal site and the second phase includes resettlement activities related to the
railway connection and the water intake line from Yellow River. A Resettlement Action
Plan (RAP) has been prepared for the first phase. The RAP for the second phase will be
prepared by mid-1997 following the completion of the design of the railway connection
and the water intake line. A separate RAP has been prepared for the Beijing T&D
component. The Bank carried out full review of the RAPs and the assessment found that
the resettlement needs of the Project-Affected Persons (PAP) are well analyzed and
methods of mitigating the adverse impacts are thoroughly formulated. The Bank's
comments on how to improve the prepared RAP are being taken into account by TEPGC
and NCPGC in finalization of their RAP prior to the appraisal mission.
3.   In connection with construction of Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant, three 500 kV
transmission lines and associated sub- and switching stations will be constructed under a
separate project which does not involve World Bank funding.  A framework of
resettlement policy and organization has been prepared by NCPGC. It is assured (a) that
the RAP for the 500 kV transmission project will be prepared in accordance with the laws
and regulations of China as well as the Guidelines of the World Bank (Operational
Directive 4.30) and (b) that the living standard of the Project-Affected Persons (PAP) will
improve or at least be restored after the project implementation.
Scope
4.    Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant.  Tuoketuo thermal power plant includes
construction of a new power plant consisting of 2 x 600 MW coal-fired units. The site of
the power plant is located in Yanshanying Township of Tuoketuo County, Huhhot City.
The project area includes power station boundary, ash yard, dedicated railroad and water



-130-                      ANNEX4.9
intake line from Yellow River which involve three counties and ten townships. The
region has vast territory and a sparse population. Except for agricultural production, no
other industry is developed. The plant site and the ash yard will cover 360 ha of land and
involve Tuoketuo County, two townships and nine villages. No public facilities and
enterprises exist in the area. The plant will require: (a) land acquisition of about 836 ha
(12,541 mu), of which 465 ha (55.6 percent) is cultivated land, and (b) demolition of 27
2
houses with a total floor space of 3,340 m . The total number of the affected persons is
2,253.
5.    Beijing T&D. Xibianmen substation is located in the inner city of Beijing. The
2
construction of Xibianmen requires acquisition of 6,100 m  of land, demolition of 239
houses, and relocation of 935 persons. It also requires demolition of five small shops
with an average area of 7 m2 and a small amount of public facilities (including 360 m of
rainwater pipe, 260 m of tapwater pipe, 270 m of heating pipe, 12 power poles, and 12
telephone wire poles). However, this program is part of a wider planned program of the
urban renovation and development of Beijing under the responsibility of Beijing
Municipal Construction Development Corporation (BMCDC). The majority of the
residential houses to be demolished are old and hazardous with poor sanitation facilities.
There is no resettlement need for Wangfujing and Xizhimen because the former is an
underground substation under construction and the latter will be built using the site of the
existing 110 kV substation. The pilot project of distribution rehabilitation involves
mainly reconductoring and installation of compact transformers and capacitors and does
not require any resettlement.
Legal Framework for Land Acquisition, Demolition, Relocation and Resettlement
6.    The Bank Requirements. The RAPs have been prepared in line with the
requirements contained in the World Bank's Operational Directive 4.30: Involuntary
Resettlement as well as applicable national and local laws and regulations.
National and Local Laws and Regulations
7.    The main state law "Land Management Law of the People's Republic of China,"
which was enacted in 1988, has been applied to the both components. The local laws and
regulations that are applied respectively to the two components are as follows.
8.    The local implementation regulations applied to Tuoketuo thermal power plant
include: Implementation of "The Land Management Law of the People's Republic of
China" issued by Inner Mongolia Autonomous Region and "Land Management Method
of Huhhot" which was ratified by the Huhhot Municipality in 1992.
9.    Local laws and regulations issued by Beijing Municipal Authorities and applied to
Beijing T&D component include: "Implementing Measures of Land Management Law
of People's Republic of China," "Fine Penalty Regulations for the Implementing
Measures of Land Management Law of People's Republic of China," and "Implementing



- 131 -                    ANNEX 4.9
Measures on Provisional Regulations of Use-Right Grant and Assignment of City and
Town State-Owned Land of People's Republic of China."
10.   During the preparation of RAPs, it was made sure that all the resettlement
activities and compensation policies are strictly governed by the applicable laws,
regulations and the Bank Guidelines.  Arrangements for relocation, prepared in
collaboration with local authorities and the population affected by the project, are in line
with Chinese national and provincial policies. Special attention was given to the most
vulnerable groups (households headed by women, senior people and poorest households).
Compensation Policies and Rates
11.   Tuoketuo Thermal Power Plant. Based on the national and local regulations of
the province and city, it is determined for the Tuoketuo Power Project that compensation
for cultivated land is 4.5 times of average output value per mu for three years before land
acquisition. Compensation for woodland will be implemented according to three times
cumulative value of grown timber and wood compensation is based on the cumulative
value of 6 m3 per mu.  For demolished and relocated houses, Tuoketuo County
Government allocated an area from the state-owned land for construction of a new village
for the PAP. TEPGC makes a financial contribution to it.
12.   The compensation rates are as follows:
Irrigated land: Y 8,336/mu
Nonirrigated land: Y 4,475/mu
Woodland: Y 3,176/mu
Subsidies for resettlement: Y 415.8/person
House: Y 612/m2
Public facility: Y 583/m2
Vegetable cellar: Y 7,500/each
Pumped well: Y 35,000/each
Brick kiln: Y 800,000/each
35kV transmission line: Y 100,000/km
10kV transmission line: Y 50,000/km
380v transmission line: Y 15,000/km
13.   Beijing T&D. The general compensation policy for residential houses is that the
resettled housing area shall not be less than the original floor space. For the residents
moved from within the second-ring-road section (inner city) into outside the third-ring-
road section, the resettled housing area shall be increased using a specified formula or a
lump sum compensation be paid off (Y 25,000-30,000). All the PAPs will be relocated
into new and higher-quality housing. Furthermore, the PAPs will be given a choice of
several resettlement locations. Compensation for the resettlement housing will be
calculated at replacement cost without depreciation.



-132-                      ANNEX4.9
14.   For residents who are living in a small house (or an apartment) with floor space
per capita below the current standard minimum living area in Beijing, the standard
minimum living area will be provided.
15.   For small shops, apart from the replacement cost of the shops, the relocation costs
and production losses during shutdown of business will also be compensated. For the
public facilities, the reconstruction (relocation) will be carried out on the basis of the
scale and quantity of the existing facilities following appropriate construction engineering
standards. Reconstruction will be completed before the existing facilities is removed.
16.   The applicable compensation rates are:
Land title: Y 4,000 /m2
House compensation, state-owned:  Y 15,000/bedroom, and private
owned: Y 20,000/bedroom
Allowance for earlier moving: Y 200/household
Allowance for moving: Y 100/bedroom
Phone relocation fee: Y 1 16/household
Compensation for TV antenna: Y 144
Compensation for school and kindergarten transfer: Y 3,000/person
Compensation for relocation to far-away areas: Y 500/person
Implementation Organization and Strategy
17.   A Project Resettlement Office with six staff members was established in May
1993 in TEPGC to oversee the management and implementation of resettlement
program. It will be assisted by Tuoketuo County Resettlement Office and Yanshanying
Township Resettlement Office. Two senior members of the office have received training
on involuntary resettlement sponsored by MOF.
18.   A Project Resettlement Office has been established to oversee the resettlement
work related to Xibianmen substation. It consists of representatives from Beijing
Municipal Power Supply Company (BMPSC), which is a division of NCPGC, BMCDC,
the Government of Xicheng District, and Beijing Municipality.
19.   For Tuoketuo thermal power plant, the new village will be constructed and made
available to PAP before December 31, 1996. After the completion of its construction and
the relocation of PAPs, demolition of the old houses will be carried out by owner
themselves. All the properties and materials of the old houses will belong to the resettled
households.
20.   The demolition and the rehabilitation of the houses will be completed before
March 1997 so that the spring plow of PAP would not be affected. Based on the
implementation plan, all PAP will be resettled near their original place. The new village
is within 300 meters of the existing village, and 250 meters of the Huhhot-Zhungeer
highway. All new houses will be built in bricks and wood. New public facilities will be



-133-                        ANNEX4.9
provided in the new village such as clinic, school, shopping and cultural centers.
Displaced farmers will continue their agricultural activities in the newly reclaimed
agricultural lands in new irrigation areas. Four motor-pumped wells will be installed for
irrigation purposes.
21.   The preparation for the construction of the new houses has already been carried
out. The design of the new house of each household affected by the project will be
carried out by the resettlement office of the county in consultation with the PAP. The
construction will be carried out by the local construction teams.
22.   The principle to minimize the resettlement of PAP as much as possible for
selection of the site and the ash yard was fully taken into consideration. Therefore, the
project will have less influence on the electrical, communication and other utility
facilities. Power supply, communication and other facilities for the construction of the
new village and for the exploitation of the new lands will be completed during the
rehabilitation. All roads through the site or ash yard will be relocated outside them. All
canals and ditches will be reconstructed outside the power plant area.
23.   Displaced households by Xibianmen substation will be relocated in new
apartment buildings with modem  facilities in a close-by residential areas, namely:
Majiabao, Donguantou, and Yalin. As housing is already commercialized in China,
NCPGC will purchase houses for the PAP in these three residential areas. All of them
can fully meet various requirement of residence in terms of comfort and convenience.
Consultation will be made on a household by household basis with the PAP regarding
their needs. All the public facilities such as road, water supply, sewage, heating, gas, and
electricity as well as auxiliary service facilities such as education, health, commerce,
garden and cultural facilities in these three areas will be completed before December
1996.

-135-                      ANNEX4.9
Resettlement Monitoring
26.   TEPGC and NCPGC respectively contracted the Inner Mongolia Academy of
Social Science (IMASS) and the Beijing Social and Psychological Research Institute
(BSPRI) to monitor the resettlement activities and provide an independent evaluation of
resettlement. The monitoring and evaluation will be based on a sample of 10 to 15
percent of affected population. The objective of monitoring and evaluation is to ensure
that the resettlement program is implemented smoothly and that the standards of living of
the PAPs are improved or at least restored during the first year following their
resettlement. The agreed outline of the first-year monitoring report includes reviewing
resettlement progress among all components; examining the use of resettlement finds;
and assessing situation regarding production restoration among relocated population, if
any; living condition improvements (housing and related services and facilities); and
administration capacity of resettlement organizations.  The group will produce a
resettlement progress report for the project office and the Bank every six months during
implementation of resettlement and annually thereafter.  After the completion of
resettlement implementation, a resettlement evaluation report will be completed.
Conflict Resolution and Grievance Procedure
27.   PAPs with grievances will be able to submit their complaints to the implementing
and supervising authorities of the project and are assured to receive a response within one
month of the submission date.

-137-                      ANNEX4.11
ANNEX 4.11: MANAGEMENT DEVELOPMENT
AND TRAINING
A. OBJECTIVES
1.    The management development and staff training program is designed to enhance
TEPGC's managerial, legal, technical and financial capabilities. The main objectives of
the program are:
(a)   to staff TEPGC with professionally skilled personnel capable of handling
power development and financial planing, power sector reform, tariff
reform, and advanced operation and maintenance techniques; and
(b)   to enable TEGPC to function as an autonomous and commercially-
oriented entity
B. SCOPE
2.    The training program will consist of the following three main categories:
(a)   training of personnel, managerial, planning, financial, legal, technical, and
environmental fields;
(b)   on-the-job training of technical staff assisted by consultants and
international experts; and
(c)   upgrading and equipping TEPGC's training facilities.
3.    High-level management, planning and financial staff will receive training in
modem management and decision-making techniques, particularly in utility management,
planning of investments, power sector reform and power pricing reform, financial
operations and management information systems. Engineering personnel will also
receive training in their specific fields, especially those related to large thermal power
construction and operation, such as advanced plant operation and preventive
maintenance, etc.
4.    Project-related training will include: (a) on-the-job training of engineering and
construction management staff by working together with the foreign consultants;
(b) training of engineering staff under the contract for major plant equipment; and
(c) training of operation and maintenance staff at other similar thermal power plants in
China and abroad. The cost of such training will be included in the equipment contracts.



-138-                       ANNEX 4.11
C. ORGANIZATION OF TRAINING
5.    TEPGC will be responsible for planning and organizing the training program with
the approval and support of concerned Chinese authorities. The training program will be
conducted both abroad and in China. Initial training activities would aim at providing a
general overview of the selected topics by a series of training seminars in China. Both
local and foreign experts will be invited to give lectures on these specific topics. Study
tours and overseas training will then be followed for senior management and financial
and technical staff.
D. IMPLEMENTATION
6.    Implementation plan for the management development and staff training program
is presented below:
(a)   Domestic Training. About 153 staff of various fields, totaling 363 staff-
months will be trained in China (Table 1); 14 staff-months of foreign
experts will be required for training in China.
(b)   Overseas Training. Study tours and overseas training will be conducted
in 1997-98 for 81 staff, totaling 162 staff-months. The number of trainees,
duration of training, staff-months and timing of different specialties of
personnel are shown in Table 1.
(c)   Project-Related Training for Technical Staff. A total of 70 experts and
technicians (a total of 140 staff-months) will be trained in manufacturers'
offices and factories. Fifteen experts and technicians (a total of 60 staff-
months) will be trained under the contract and agreement for consulting
services.  Operation and maintenance training for 200 experts and
technicians (a total of 600 staff-months) will be provided in China in
NCPGC and IMEPC training facilities.
(d)   Training Equipment. Equipment to be purchased are given in Table 3.
(e)   Estimated Training Cost. The total training cost will be Y 13.4 million
equivalent in local currency and 1.57 million in foreign currency (Tables
1-4).

and the ash handling plant;
(b)   Turbine-generator island  (including  condensing  and  feed-heating
equipment, condensate polishing plant, step-up transformer, isolated phase
bus ducts and hydrogen generating equipment).
3.    The following procurement packages will be financed by commercial cofinancing
sources. For the procurement of those contracts for goods and works not financed by the
Bank loan, the Borrower may adopt other procedures. In such cases the Bank shall be
satisfied that the procedures to be used will fulfill the Borrower's obligations to cause the
project to be carried out diligently and efficiently. (Refer to paras. 1.5 and 3.14 of the
"Guidelines for Procurement Under IBRD Loans and IDA Credits," January 1995,
revised in January and August of 1996.)
(a)   Instrumentation and control island, including on-line performance
monitor;
(b)   500 kV electrical equipment within the power station boundary (six SF6
circuit breakers, etc.);
(c)   Ash handling plant;
(d)   Construction equipment (including the 250 ton crawler crane);
(e)   Construction material (steel, 580 tons);
(f)   Operator training simulator;
(g)   Other miscellaneous packages for communication systems, HVAC, the
water treatment system, etc.

l~ The commercial operation of the first unit is scheduled on October 1, 2001. The availability of the unit is calculated as
1- (Forced Outage Hours + Scheduled Outage Hours )/ Total Hours in the Period
Total hours in the first year are counted from the starting of the commercial operation to the end of the year. In the
subsequent years, total hours in the period = 8760 hours.
Lb The commercial operation of the second unit is scheduled on September 1, 2002.
I Interruption hours* per distribution transformer (10 kV) =
Y Interruption hours x Number of interrupted distribution transformers
Total number of distribution transformers
* Load shedding not included
Ld Voltage variation =
1-  Minutes outside the allowed voltage variation range / (Total minutes in the period x number of samples)
Allowed voltage variation range:
* Standard supply voltage: 10 kV, upper limit 10.7 kV, lower limit 9.8 kV
* Standard supply voltage: 380/220V for motor, + 7%
* Standard supply voltage, 380/220V for lighting, + 7%, - 10%
Voltage variation is monitored on a continuous basis for all voltage levels (110 kV, 35 kV, 10 kV, and 380/220 V). A total
of 500 samples are taken, of which 140 for 380/220 V.

-154-                      ANNEX5.2
ANNEX 5.2: MAJOR ASSUMPTIONS FOR TEPGC'S
FINANCIAL PROJECTIONS
A. GENERAL
1.    The general inflation rates are assumed as follows:
Local: 14.8 percent for 1995, 10.0 for 1996, 8.0 for 1997, 7.0 for 1998, 6.5 for
1999 and thereafter.
Foreign: 2.6 percent for 1995, 2.9 for 1996, 2.0 for 1997, 2.1 for 1998, 2.3 for
1999, 2.4 for 2000, 2.3 for 2001, 2.2 for 2002, 2.2 for 2003, 2.3 for
2004, 2.2 for 2005 and thereafter.
2.    The foreign exchange rate used is $1 = Y 8.3257.
3.    The interest rates for local loans and IBRD loan are assumed to be 13.01 percent
and 5.89 percent per year, respectively. The IBRD loan would be repayable in 20 years
including a 5-year grace period. The commercial loans under the cofinancing program
are assumed to bear an interest rate of 6.5 percent and repayable in 15 years, including 5
years' grace.
B. INCOME STATEMENTS
4.    Energy sales is calculated based on total available capacity, load factor, station
usage and transmission loss before the main transformer.
5.    The tariffs are assumed to be adjusted so that the average revenues would be
adequate for achieving the minimum financial performance targets.
6.    The annual depreciation rate is assumed to be 4.75 percent.
7.    All interest during construction (IDC) are capitalized.
8.    The average wages are assumed to increase by 5 percent in real terms per year
based on 1995's actual, Y 11,000, and benefits are assumed to be 14 percent of the total
wages.
9.    The total number of employee is assumed to be 600 based on an coefficient of
0.5 person/MW.
10.   Fuel costs are assumed to increase by 3 percent per year in real terms based on
1995's actual, Y 135/ton, until 2000 and escalate with the local inflation rates thereafter.



-155-                       ANNEX5.2
11.   Under the operation and maintenance costs, material (Y 0.007 million/GWh in
1995) and water (Y 0.0013 million/GWh in 1995) costs are assumed to escalate with
local inflation rates; and maintenance cost is assumed to be 1.5 percent of fixed assets.
The administration expenses are assumed to escalate with local inflation rate based on a
coefficient of Y 0.011 million/GWh.
12.   Income tax is expected to be assessed at 33 percent of taxable income.
13.   Value-added tax (VAT) is 17 percent and the effective rate is assumed to be 8.5
percent after deducting VAT included in the costs for fuel and materials.
14.   Urban and education tax rates are 7 and 3 percent of VAT, respectively.
C. BALANCE SHEET
15.   Inventories are assumed to be half a month's fuel supply plus I percent of fixed
assets.
16.   Accounts receivable is assumed to be maintained at one month's operating
revenue (including VAT).
17.   Fixed assets cost includes estimated total project costs, capitalized interest during
construction, and commitment fees. No annual revaluation of fixed assets is assumed.
18.   Accounts payable is assumed to cover 45 days' cash operating expenses.
19.   Short-term loans are equivalent to 3 months of current assets excluding cash.
20.   Paid-in capital will not change over time unless new shares are issued or more
equity contributions are made from investors.
21.   Earned surplus included accumulated legal accumulation funds and welfare
funds that appropriated from net income each year.
22.   Retained earnings will increase by each year's net income and decrease by the
above two appropriations and declared dividends.

-163 -                      ANNEX 5.5
ANNEX 5.5: MAJOR ASSUMPTIONS FOR NCPGC'S
FINANCIAL PROJECTIONS
A. GENERAL
1.    The general inflation rates are assumed as follows:
Local: 14.8 percent for 1995, 10.0 for 1996, 8.0 for 1997, 7.0 for 1998, 6.5 for
1999 and thereafter.
Foreign: 2.6 percent for 1995, 2.9 for 1996, 2.0 for 1997, 2.1 for 1998, 2.3 for
1999, 2.4 for 2000, 2.3 for 2001, 2.2 for 2002, 2.2 for 2003, 2.3 for
2004, 2.2 for 2005 and thereafter.
2.    The foreign exchange rate used is $1 = Y 8.3257.
3.    The interest rates for local loans and IBRD loan are assumed to be 13.01 percent
and 5.89 percent per year, respectively. The IBRD loan would be repayable in 20 years
including a 5-year grace period.
4.    The capital investment program is based on the least-cost power development
planning for NCPGC.
B. INCOME STATEMENTS
5.    Energy sales projection is calculated based on load forecast by NCPGC. Energy
sales is assumed to grow by 8 percent per year during the period 1995-2003.
6.    The tariffs are assumed to be adjusted so that the average revenues would be
adequate for achieving the minimum financial performance targets.
7.    The actual average consumption rate of standard coal in 1995 for generation
was 347.5 g/kWh. The rate is assumed to decline to about 332 g/kWh by 2003.
8.    The cost of purchased power is assumed to increase by 3 percent per year in real
terms based on 1995 actual. The purchase price for the power from Tuoketuo thermal
power plant is based on the power purchase agreement between TEPGC and NCPGC.
9.    The average line loss rate of NCPGC is assumed to be 8 percent.
10.   The annual depreciation rate is assumed to be 6.6 percent.
11.   All interest during construction (IDC) are capitalized.



-164 -                      ANNEX 5.5
12.   The average wages are assumed to increase by 5 percent per year in real terms
based on 1995's actual plus half of the growth rate of energy sales.
13.   The total number of employee is assumed to increase by 2 percent a year.
14.   Fuel costs are assumed to increase by 2 percent per year in real terms based on
1995's actual, Y 219/ton, till 2003.
15.   Under the operation and maintenance costs, material cost is assumed to increase
by 5 percent plus the rate of growth of original fixed assets per year in real terms; water
cost is assumed to increase by 5 percent plus the rate of growth of electricity generated
per year in real terms; and maintenance cost is assumed to be 2.5 percent of fixed assets.
16.   Income tax is expected to be assessed at 33 percent of taxable income.
17.   Value-added tax (VAT) is 17 percent and the effective rate is assumed to be 9.4
percent after deducting VAT included in the costs for fuel and materials.
18.   Urban and education tax rates are 7 and 3 percent of VAT, respectively.
C. BALANCE SHEET
19.   Inventories are assumed to be half-a-month's fuel supply plus 2 percent of the
gross fixed assets.
20.   Accounts receivable is assumed to be maintained at 18 days' gross sales revenue
in 1996 and to be reduced gradually to 12 days by 2003.
21.   Other accounts receivable is assumed to increase by 8 percent per year.
22.   Fixed assets cost includes estimated total project costs, capitalized interest during
construction, and commitment fees. No annual revaluation of fixed assets is assumed.
23.   Accounts payable is assumed to decrease gradually from 44 days of costs for
fuel, purchased power, and materials in 1996 to 26 days by 2003.
24.   Tax payable is assumed to be reduced from 40 days of effective VAT and other
surcharges in 1996 to 35 days by 2003.
25.   Short-term loans are equivalent to 2 months of current assets excluding cash.
26.   Paid-in capital will not change over time unless new shares are issued or more
equity contributions are made from investors.
27.   Earned surplus included accumulated legal accumulation funds and welfare
funds that appropriated from net income each year.



- 165 -                     ANNEX 5.5
28.   Retained earnings will increase by each year's net income and decrease by the
above two appropriations and declared dividends.
D. FUNDS FLOW STATEMENT
29.   The consumer contributions represents the receipts of consumer comnections and
is assumed to increase by annual energy sales growth rate based on 1995 actual
collection.
